# Text Elements
To construct the regular expression of [^A], we must first construct the FA for the regular expression A.
Then we must invert the final and non-final nodes of the FA obtained for the regular expression A to get the FA of [^A].
ie: final -> non-final, non-final -> final
Finally, we convert it back into a regular expression with no complement using Kleene's Theorem.
FA -> NFA -> GNFA -> regular


For example: to construct [^aB], let  
we first construct the FA for the regular expression a|B.


 ^TcLiWxLC

to obtain the complement of [aB], which is [^aB]
we invert the final and non-final nodes.
 ^lDwW75Gu

finally we can convert this FA into an equivalent regular expression, which does not use complement.
We convert through the steps for Kleene's Theorem.
FA -> NFA -> GFA -> regular expression ^QnH50jNU
